<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Nursing</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Health care profession</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Nursing_(disambiguation)" title="Nursing (disambiguation)">Nursing (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Nurse" and "Nurses" redirect here. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Nurse_(disambiguation)" title="Nurse (disambiguation)">Nurse (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066479718">.mw-parser-output .infobox-subbox{padding:0;border:none;margin:-3px;width:auto;min-width:100%;font-size:100%;clear:none;float:none;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .infobox-3cols-child{margin:auto}.mw-parser-output .infobox .navbar{font-size:100%}body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-header,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-subheader,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-above,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-title,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-image,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-full-data,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-below{text-align:center}</style><table class="infobox"><caption class="infobox-title">Nursing</caption><tbody><tr><th class="infobox-header" colspan="2">Occupation</th></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row"><div style="display: inline-block; line-height: 1.2em; padding: .1em 0;">Activity sectors</div></th><td class="infobox-data">Nursing</td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-header" colspan="2">Description</th></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row">Competencies</th><td class="infobox-data">Caring for general and specialized well-being of patients</td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row"><div style="display: inline-block; line-height: 1.2em; padding: .1em 0;">Education required</div></th><td class="infobox-data">Qualifications in terms of statutory regulations according to national, state, or provincial legislation in each country</td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row"><div style="display: inline-block; line-height: 1.2em; padding: .1em 0;">Fields of<br/>employment</div></th><td class="infobox-data">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Hospital" title="Hospital">Hospital</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Clinic" title="Clinic">Clinic</a></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">Education</a></li>

</td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row"><div style="display: inline-block; line-height: 1.2em; padding: .1em 0;">Related jobs</div></th><td class="infobox-data">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">Medicine</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_medicine" title="Glossary of medicine">Glossary of medicine</a></li></ul>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Nursing</b> is a profession within the <a href="/wiki/Health_care" title="Health care">health care</a> sector focused on the care of individuals, families, and communities so they may attain, maintain, or recover optimal health and <a href="/wiki/Quality_of_life_(healthcare)" title="Quality of life (healthcare)">quality of life</a>. They also take on vital roles of education, assessing situations, as support.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-:5-1">[1]</a></sup> Nurses may be differentiated from other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Health_care_providers" title="Health care providers">health care providers</a> by their <a href="/wiki/Nursing_theory" title="Nursing theory">approach to patient care</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nurse_education" title="Nurse education">training</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Scope_of_practice" title="Scope of practice">scope of practice</a>. Nurses practice in many <a href="/wiki/List_of_nursing_specialties" title="List of nursing specialties">specialties</a> with differing levels of <a href="/wiki/Medical_prescription" title="Medical prescription">prescription authority</a>. Nurses comprise the largest component of most healthcare environments;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> but there is evidence of international shortages of qualified nurses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> Many nurses provide care within the ordering scope of <a href="/wiki/Physician" title="Physician">physicians</a>, and this traditional role has shaped the public image of nurses as care providers. Nurse practitioners are nurses with a graduate degree in advanced practice nursing. They are however permitted by most jurisdictions to practice independently in a variety of settings. Since the <a href="/wiki/Post-war" title="Post-war">postwar</a> period, nurse education has undergone a process of diversification towards <a href="/wiki/Nursing_credentials_and_certifications" title="Nursing credentials and certifications">advanced and specialized credentials</a>, and many of the traditional regulations and provider roles are changing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup>
</p><p>Nurses develop a plan of care, working collaboratively with physicians, therapists, the patient, the patient's family, and other team members that focuses on treating illness to improve quality of life. In the United Kingdom and the United States, clinical nurse specialists and nurse practitioners, diagnose health problems and prescribe the correct medications and other therapies, depending on particular state regulations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Nurses may help coordinate the patient care performed by other members of a multidisciplinary health care team such as therapists, medical practitioners, and dietitians. Nurses provide care both interdependently, for example, with physicians, and independently as nursing professionals. In addition to providing care and support, nurses educate the public, and promote health and wellness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup>
</p>

<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-59"><a href="#Taiwan"><span class="tocnumber">8.3.5</span> <span class="toctext">Taiwan</span></a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-60"><a href="#Australia"><span class="tocnumber">8.4</span> <span class="toctext">Australia</span></a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-61"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_nursing" title="History of nursing">History of nursing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_nursing_history" title="Timeline of nursing history">Timeline of nursing history</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Premodern">Premodern</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Premodern">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Nursing historians face the challenges of determining whether care provided to the sick or injured in antiquity is called nursing care.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OLYNN2007_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-OLYNN2007-9">[9]</a></sup> In the fifth century BC, for example, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hippocratic_Collection" title="Hippocratic Collection">Hippocratic Collection</a> in places describes skilled care and observation of patients by male "attendants," who may have been early nurses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LEVINE1965_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-LEVINE1965-10">[10]</a></sup> Around 600 BC in India, it is recorded in <a href="/wiki/Sushruta_Samhita" title="Sushruta Samhita">Sushruta Samhita</a>, Book 3, Chapter V about the role of the nurse as "the different parts or members of the body as mentioned before including the skin, cannot be correctly described by one who is not well versed in anatomy. Hence, any one desirous of acquiring a thorough knowledge of anatomy should prepare a dead body and carefully, observe, by dissecting it, and examine its different parts."
</p><p>Before the foundation of modern nursing, members of religious orders such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nuns" title="Nuns">nuns</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monks" title="Monks">monks</a> often provided nursing-like care.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BLOY_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-BLOY-11">[11]</a></sup> Examples exist in <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FERNGREN2009_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FERNGREN2009-12">[12]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamic" title="Islamic">Islamic</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SACHEDINA2009_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-SACHEDINA2009-13">[13]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhist" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DEBARY2011_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-DEBARY2011-14">[14]</a></sup> traditions amongst others. <a href="/wiki/Phoebe_(biblical_figure)" title="Phoebe (biblical figure)">Phoebe</a>, mentioned in <a href="/wiki/Epistle_to_the_Romans" title="Epistle to the Romans">Romans</a> 16 has been described in many sources as "the first visiting nurse".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EGENES2009_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-EGENES2009-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-STRIEPE1992_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-STRIEPE1992-16">[16]</a></sup> These traditions were influential in the development of the <a href="/wiki/Ethos" title="Ethos">ethos</a> of modern nursing. The religious roots of modern nursing remain in evidence today in many countries. One example in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> is the use of the historical title "sister" to refer to a senior nurse in the past.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WAND2004_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-WAND2004-17">[17]</a></sup>
</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Reformation" title="Reformation">Reformation</a> of the 16th century, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> reformers shut down the monasteries and convents, allowing a few hundred municipal hospices to remain in operation in northern Europe. Those nuns who had been serving as nurses were given pensions or told to get married and stay home.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Nursing care went to the inexperienced as traditional caretakers, rooted in the Roman Catholic Church, were removed from their positions. The nursing profession suffered a major setback for approximately 200 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="19th_century">19th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 19th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A1%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D1%8B_%D0%9A%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%B4%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%BE%D0%B1%D1%89%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%8B,_%D0%A1%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C,_1855.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2026" data-file-width="2842" decoding="async" height="121" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/%D0%A1%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D1%8B_%D0%9A%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%B4%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%BE%D0%B1%D1%89%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%8B%2C_%D0%A1%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%2C_1855.jpg/170px-%D0%A1%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D1%8B_%D0%9A%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%B4%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%BE%D0%B1%D1%89%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%8B%2C_%D0%A1%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%2C_1855.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/%D0%A1%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D1%8B_%D0%9A%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%B4%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%BE%D0%B1%D1%89%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%8B%2C_%D0%A1%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%2C_1855.jpg/255px-%D0%A1%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D1%8B_%D0%9A%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%B4%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%BE%D0%B1%D1%89%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%8B%2C_%D0%A1%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%2C_1855.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/%D0%A1%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D1%8B_%D0%9A%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%B4%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%BE%D0%B1%D1%89%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%8B%2C_%D0%A1%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%2C_1855.jpg/340px-%D0%A1%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D1%8B_%D0%9A%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%B4%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%BE%D0%B1%D1%89%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%8B%2C_%D0%A1%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%2C_1855.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A1%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D1%8B_%D0%9A%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%B4%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%BE%D0%B1%D1%89%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%8B,_%D0%A1%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C,_1855.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Russian Sisters of Mercy in the Crimea, 1854-1855</div></div></div>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a> the <a href="/wiki/Princess_Charlotte_of_W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Princess Charlotte of Württemberg">Grand Duchess Elena Pavlovna</a> issued the call for women to join the Order of Exaltation of the Cross (Krestodvizhenskaya obshchina) for the year of service in the military hospitals. The first section of twenty-eight "sisters", headed by Aleksandra Petrovna Stakhovich, the Directress of the Order, went off to the Crimea early in November 1854.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Florence_Nightingale_(H_Hering_NPG_x82368).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="1105" decoding="async" height="236" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Florence_Nightingale_%28H_Hering_NPG_x82368%29.jpg/170px-Florence_Nightingale_%28H_Hering_NPG_x82368%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Florence_Nightingale_%28H_Hering_NPG_x82368%29.jpg/255px-Florence_Nightingale_%28H_Hering_NPG_x82368%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Florence_Nightingale_%28H_Hering_NPG_x82368%29.jpg/340px-Florence_Nightingale_%28H_Hering_NPG_x82368%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Florence_Nightingale_(H_Hering_NPG_x82368).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Florence_Nightingale" title="Florence Nightingale">Florence Nightingale</a> was an influential figure in the development of modern nursing. No uniform had been created when Nightingale was employed during the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a>. Often considered the first nurse theorist, Nightingale linked health with five environmental factors:(1) pure or fresh air, (2) pure water, (3) efficient drainage, (4) cleanliness, and (5) light, especially direct sunlight. Deficiencies in these five factors resulted in a lack of health or illness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Both the role of nursing and education were first defined by Nightingale.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Florence_Nightingale" title="Florence Nightingale">Florence Nightingale</a> laid the foundations of professional nursing after the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WINKEL2009_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-WINKEL2009-22">[22]</a></sup> Nightingale believed that nursing was a social freedom and mission for women. She believed that any educated woman can help improve the care of the medically sick.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Her <i><a href="/wiki/Notes_on_Nursing" title="Notes on Nursing">Notes on Nursing</a></i> (1859) became popular. The Nightingale model of professional education, having set up one of the <a href="/wiki/Florence_Nightingale_Faculty_of_Nursing_and_Midwifery" title="Florence Nightingale Faculty of Nursing and Midwifery">first schools of nursing</a> that is connected to a continuously operating hospital and medical school, spread widely in Europe and North America after 1870.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Quinn_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Quinn-24">[24]</a></sup> Nightingale was also a pioneer of the graphical presentation of <a href="/wiki/Statistics" title="Statistics">statistical</a> <a href="/wiki/Data" title="Data">data</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup>
</p><p>Florence Nightingale worked by sub concepts of the environmental theory. She included five factors that helped nurses in her time of working in poor sanitation and with uneducated nurses. These factors included (1) fresh air, (2) clean water, (3) a working drainage system, (4) cleanliness, and (5) good light or sunlight. Nightingale believed that a clean, working environment were important in caring for patients. In the 19th century, this theory was ideal for helping patients, providing a guide for nurses to alter the environment around the patient for the better of their health.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup>
</p><p>Nightingale's recommendations built upon the successes of Jamaican "doctresses" such as <a href="/wiki/Mary_Seacole" title="Mary Seacole">Mary Seacole</a>, who like Nightingale, served in the Crimean War. Seacole practised hygiene and the use of herbs in healing wounded soldiers and those suffering from diseases in the 19th century in the Crimea, Central America, and Jamaica. Her predecessors had great success as healers in the <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Jamaica" title="Colony of Jamaica">Colony of Jamaica</a> in the 18th century, and they included Seacole's mother, Mrs. Grant, Sarah Adams, <a href="/wiki/Cubah_Cornwallis" title="Cubah Cornwallis">Cubah Cornwallis</a>, and Grace Donne, the mistress and doctress to Jamaica's wealthiest planter, <a href="/wiki/Simon_Taylor_(sugar_planter)" title="Simon Taylor (sugar planter)">Simon Taylor</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup>
</p><p>Other important nurses in the development of the profession include:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Agnes_Hunt" title="Agnes Hunt">Agnes Hunt</a> from <a href="/wiki/Shropshire" title="Shropshire">Shropshire</a> was the first orthopedic nurse and was pivotal in the emergence of the orthopedic hospital The Robert Jones &amp; Agnes Hunt Hospital in Oswestry, Shropshire.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Val%C3%A9rie_de_Gasparin" title="Valérie de Gasparin">Valérie de Gasparin</a> who opened, with her husband <a href="/wiki/Ag%C3%A9nor_de_Gasparin" title="Agénor de Gasparin">Agénor de Gasparin</a>, the first nursing school in the world : <a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Institut_et_haute_%C3%A9cole_de_la_sant%C3%A9_La_Source" title="fr:Institut et haute école de la santé La Source">La Source</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Lausanne" title="Lausanne">Lausanne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Agnes_Jones" title="Agnes Jones">Agnes Jones</a>, who established a nurse training regime at the <a href="/wiki/Brownlow_Hill_infirmary" title="Brownlow Hill infirmary">Brownlow Hill infirmary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a>, in 1865.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Linda_Richards" title="Linda Richards">Linda Richards</a>, who established quality <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nursing_schools" title="Nursing schools">nursing schools</a> in the United States and Japan, and was officially the first professionally trained nurse in the US, graduating in 1873 from the <i><a href="/wiki/New_England_Hospital_for_Women_and_Children" title="New England Hospital for Women and Children">New England Hospital for Women and Children</a></i> in Boston.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Clara_Barton" title="Clara Barton">Clarissa Harlowe "Clara" Barton</a>, a pioneer American teacher, patent clerk, nurse, and humanitarian, and the founder of the American Red Cross.</li>
<li>Saint <a href="/wiki/Marianne_Cope" title="Marianne Cope">Marianne Cope</a>, a Sister of St. Francis who opened and operated some of the first general hospitals in the United States, instituting cleanliness standards which influenced the development of America's modern hospital system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></li></ul>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_Cross" title="Red Cross">Red Cross</a> chapters, which began appearing after the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/International_Committee_of_the_Red_Cross" title="International Committee of the Red Cross">International Committee of the Red Cross</a> in 1863, offered employment and professionalization opportunities for nurses (despite initial objections from <a href="/wiki/Florence_Nightingale" title="Florence Nightingale">Florence Nightingale</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Catholic orders such as <a href="/wiki/Little_Sisters_of_the_Poor" title="Little Sisters of the Poor">Little Sisters of the Poor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sisters_of_Mercy" title="Sisters of Mercy">Sisters of Mercy</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sisters_of_St._Mary" title="Sisters of St. Mary">Sisters of St. Mary</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Franciscan_Alliance,_Inc." title="Franciscan Alliance, Inc.">St. Francis Health Services, Inc.</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sisters_of_Charity" title="Sisters of Charity">Sisters of Charity</a> built hospitals and provided nursing services during this period.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> In turn, the modern deaconess movement began in Germany in 1836.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NAUMANN2008_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-NAUMANN2008-31">[31]</a></sup> Within a half century, there were over 5,000 deaconesses in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BLACKMORE2007_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-BLACKMORE2007-32">[32]</a></sup>
</p><p>Formal use of nurses in the modern military began in the latter half of the nineteenth century. Nurses saw active duty in the <a href="/wiki/First_Boer_War" title="First Boer War">First Boer War</a>, the Egyptian Campaign (1882),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Mahdist_War" title="Mahdist War">Sudan Campaign</a> (1883).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Women_in_nursing" title="Women in nursing">Women in nursing</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RedCrossNursen.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3500" data-file-width="2614" decoding="async" height="295" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/RedCrossNursen.jpg/220px-RedCrossNursen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/RedCrossNursen.jpg/330px-RedCrossNursen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/RedCrossNursen.jpg/440px-RedCrossNursen.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RedCrossNursen.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A recruiting poster for Australian nurses from <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a></div></div></div>
<p>Hospital-based training came to the fore in the early 1900s, with an emphasis on practical experience. The Nightingale-style school began to disappear. Hospitals and physicians saw women in nursing as a source of free or inexpensive labor. Exploitation of nurses was not uncommon by employers, physicians, and educational providers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CHIN2008_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-CHIN2008-35">[35]</a></sup>
</p><p>Many nurses saw active duty in <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, but the profession was transformed during the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a>. British nurses of the Army Nursing Service were part of every overseas campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> More nurses volunteered for service in the US <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">Army</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">Navy</a> than any other occupation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The Nazis had their own Brown Nurses, 40,000 strong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Two dozen German Red Cross nurses were awarded the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Cross" title="Iron Cross">Iron Cross</a> for heroism under fire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup>
</p><p>The modern era saw the development of undergraduate and post-graduate <a href="/wiki/Nurse_education" title="Nurse education">nursing degrees</a>. Advancement of nursing research and a desire for association and organization led to the formation of a wide variety of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Professional_organizations" title="Professional organizations">professional organizations</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nursing_journal" title="Nursing journal">academic journals</a>. Growing recognition of nursing as a distinct academic discipline was accompanied by an awareness of the need to define the <a href="/wiki/Nursing_theory" title="Nursing theory">theoretical basis</a> for practice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ALLIGOOD2013_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-ALLIGOOD2013-41">[41]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 19th and early 20th century, nursing was considered a women's profession, just as doctoring was a men's profession. With increasing expectations of workplace equality during the late 20th century, nursing became an officially <a href="/wiki/Gender_marking_in_job_titles" title="Gender marking in job titles">gender-neutral</a> profession, though in practice the percentage of male nurses remains well below that of female <a href="/wiki/Physician" title="Physician">physicians</a> in the early 21st century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Shortages">Shortages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Shortages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The biggest shortages of nurses and midwives are in South East Asia and Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> A global survey by <a href="/wiki/McKinsey_%26_Company" title="McKinsey &amp; Company">McKinsey &amp; Company</a> in 2022 found that between 28% and 38% of nurse respondents in the United States, the United Kingdom, Singapore, Japan, and France said they were likely to leave their current role in direct patient care in the next year. Nursing shortages are a rising risk in many countries. The top five factors which they said would make them stay were
</p>
<ul><li>A safe working environment</li>
<li>Work-life balance</li>
<li>Caring and trusting team-mates</li>
<li>Doing meaningful work</li>
<li>Flexible work schedule</li></ul>
<p>Pay was eighth on the list.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup>  An American survey in 2003 found about half the respondents were considering leaving.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definition">Definition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Definition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Although nursing practice varies both through its various specialties and countries, these nursing organizations offer the following definitions:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p> Nursing encompasses autonomous and collaborative care of individuals of all ages, families, groups and communities, sick or well, and in all settings. Nursing includes the promotion of health, prevention of illness, and the care of ill, disabled and dying people. Advocacy, promotion of a safe environment, research, participation in shaping health policy and in patient and health systems management, and education are also key nursing roles. </p><div class="templatequotecite">— <cite><a href="/wiki/International_Council_of_Nurses" title="International Council of Nurses">International Council of Nurses</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICN_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-ICN-47">[47]</a></sup></cite></div></blockquote>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The use of clinical judgment in the provision of care to enable people to improve, maintain, or recover health, to cope with health problems, and to achieve the best possible quality of life, whatever their disease or disability, until death.</p><div class="templatequotecite">— <cite><a href="/wiki/Royal_College_of_Nursing" title="Royal College of Nursing">Royal College of Nursing</a> (2003) <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></cite></div></blockquote>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Nursing is the protection, promotion, and optimization of health and abilities; prevention of illness and injury; alleviation of suffering through the diagnosis and treatment of human responses; and advocacy in health care for individuals, families, communities, and populations.</p><div class="templatequotecite">— <cite><a href="/wiki/American_Nurses_Association" title="American Nurses Association">American Nurses Association</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></cite></div></blockquote>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The unique function of the nurse is to assist the individual, sick or well, in the performance of those activities contributing to health or its recovery (or to peaceful death) that he would perform unaided if he had the necessary strength, will or knowledge.</p><div class="templatequotecite">— <cite><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virginia_Avenel_Henderson" title="Virginia Avenel Henderson">Virginia Avenel Henderson</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></cite></div></blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="As_a_profession">As a profession</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: As a profession">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Indonesian_nurse_examines_patient.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Indonesian_nurse_examines_patient.JPG/220px-Indonesian_nurse_examines_patient.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Indonesian_nurse_examines_patient.JPG/330px-Indonesian_nurse_examines_patient.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Indonesian_nurse_examines_patient.JPG/440px-Indonesian_nurse_examines_patient.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Indonesian_nurse_examines_patient.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A nurse in Indonesia examining a patient</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ASC_Leiden_-_Coutinho_Collection_-_10_04_-_Nurses_in_Ziguinchor_hospital,_Senegal_-_1973.tif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4788" data-file-width="3222" decoding="async" height="327" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/ASC_Leiden_-_Coutinho_Collection_-_10_04_-_Nurses_in_Ziguinchor_hospital%2C_Senegal_-_1973.tif/lossy-page1-220px-ASC_Leiden_-_Coutinho_Collection_-_10_04_-_Nurses_in_Ziguinchor_hospital%2C_Senegal_-_1973.tif.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/ASC_Leiden_-_Coutinho_Collection_-_10_04_-_Nurses_in_Ziguinchor_hospital%2C_Senegal_-_1973.tif/lossy-page1-330px-ASC_Leiden_-_Coutinho_Collection_-_10_04_-_Nurses_in_Ziguinchor_hospital%2C_Senegal_-_1973.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/ASC_Leiden_-_Coutinho_Collection_-_10_04_-_Nurses_in_Ziguinchor_hospital%2C_Senegal_-_1973.tif/lossy-page1-440px-ASC_Leiden_-_Coutinho_Collection_-_10_04_-_Nurses_in_Ziguinchor_hospital%2C_Senegal_-_1973.tif.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ASC_Leiden_-_Coutinho_Collection_-_10_04_-_Nurses_in_Ziguinchor_hospital,_Senegal_-_1973.tif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A nurse treating a patient with burns, <a href="/wiki/Ziguinchor" title="Ziguinchor">Ziguinchor</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PAIGC" title="PAIGC">PAIGC</a> hospital, 1973</div></div></div>
<p>The authority for the practice of nursing is based upon a social contract that delineates professional rights and responsibilities as well as mechanisms for public accountability. In almost all countries, nursing practice is defined and governed by law, and entrance to the profession is regulated at the national or state level.
</p><p>The aim of the nursing community worldwide is for its professionals to ensure quality care for all, while maintaining their credentials, code of <a href="/wiki/Nursing_ethics" title="Nursing ethics">ethics</a>, standards, and competencies, and continuing their education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICN_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-ICN-47">[47]</a></sup> There are a number of educational paths to becoming a professional nurse, which vary greatly worldwide; all involve extensive study of <a href="/wiki/Nursing_theory" title="Nursing theory">nursing theory</a> and practice as well as training in clinical skills.
</p><p>Nurses care for individuals of all ages and cultural backgrounds who are healthy and ill in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holistic_health" title="Holistic health">holistic</a> manner based on the individual's physical, emotional, psychological, intellectual, social, and spiritual needs. The profession combines physical science, social science, nursing theory, and technology in caring for those individuals.
</p><p>To work in the nursing profession, all nurses hold one or more credentials depending on their <a href="/wiki/Scope_of_practice" title="Scope of practice">scope of practice</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nurse_education" title="Nurse education">education</a>. In the United States, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Licensed_Practical_Nurse" title="Licensed Practical Nurse">Licensed Practical Nurse</a> (LPN) works independently or with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Registered_Nurse" title="Registered Nurse">Registered Nurse</a> (RN). The most significant difference between an LPN and RN is found in the requirements for entry to practice, which determines entitlement for their scope of practice. RNs provide scientific, psychological, and technological knowledge in the care of patients and families in many health care settings. RNs may earn additional <a href="/wiki/Nursing_credentials_and_certifications" title="Nursing credentials and certifications">credentials</a> or <a href="/wiki/Academic_degree" title="Academic degree">degrees</a>.
</p><p>In the United States, multiple educational paths will qualify a candidate to sit for the licensure examination as an RN. The <a href="#Associate_Degree_in_Nursing">Associate Degree in Nursing</a> (ADN) is awarded to the nurse who has completed a two-year undergraduate academic degree awarded by community colleges, junior colleges, technical colleges, and bachelor's degree-granting colleges and universities upon completion of a course of study usually lasting two years. It is also referred to as Associate in Nursing (AN), Associate of Applied Science in Nursing (AAS), or Associate of Science in Nursing (ASN).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> The <a href="#Bachelor_of_Science_in_Nursing">Bachelor of Science in Nursing</a> (BSN) is awarded to the nurse who has earned an American four-year academic degree in the science and principles of nursing, granted by a tertiary education university or similarly accredited school. After completing either the LPN or either RN education programs in the United States, graduates are eligible to sit for a licensing examination to become a nurse, the passing of which is required for the nursing license. The <a href="/wiki/National_Council_Licensure_Examination" title="National Council Licensure Examination">National Licensure Examination</a> (NCLEX) test is a standardized exam (including multiple choice, select all that apply, fill in the blank and "hot spot" questions) that nurses take to become licensed. It costs two-hundred dollars to take and examines a nurses ability to properly care for a client. Study books and practice tests are available for purchase.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some nurses follow the traditional role of working in a hospital setting. Other options include: pediatrics, neonatal, maternity, OBGYN, geriatrics, ambulatory, and nurse anesthetists and informatics (<a href="/wiki/EHealth" title="EHealth">eHealth</a>). There are many other options nurses can explore depending on the type of degree and education acquired. These options can also include, community health, mental health, clinical nursing specialists, and nurse midwives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> RNs may also pursue different roles as <a href="/wiki/Advanced_practice_nurse" title="Advanced practice nurse">advanced practice nurses</a>.
</p><p>Nurses are not doctors' assistants. This is possible in certain situations, but nurses more often are independently caring for their patients or assisting other nurses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> RNs treat patients, record their medical history, provide emotional support, and provide follow-up care. Nurses also help doctors perform diagnostic tests. Nurses are almost always working on their own or with other nurses. However, they also assist doctors in the emergency room or in trauma care when help is needed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gender_issues">Gender issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Gender issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Men_in_nursing" title="Men in nursing">Men in nursing</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Male_Nurses-_Life_at_Runwell_Hospital,_Wickford,_Essex,_1943_D14313.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="757" decoding="async" height="211" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Male_Nurses-_Life_at_Runwell_Hospital%2C_Wickford%2C_Essex%2C_1943_D14313.jpg/200px-Male_Nurses-_Life_at_Runwell_Hospital%2C_Wickford%2C_Essex%2C_1943_D14313.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Male_Nurses-_Life_at_Runwell_Hospital%2C_Wickford%2C_Essex%2C_1943_D14313.jpg/300px-Male_Nurses-_Life_at_Runwell_Hospital%2C_Wickford%2C_Essex%2C_1943_D14313.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Male_Nurses-_Life_at_Runwell_Hospital%2C_Wickford%2C_Essex%2C_1943_D14313.jpg/400px-Male_Nurses-_Life_at_Runwell_Hospital%2C_Wickford%2C_Essex%2C_1943_D14313.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Male_Nurses-_Life_at_Runwell_Hospital,_Wickford,_Essex,_1943_D14313.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A nurse at Runwell Hospital, Wickford, Essex, in 1943</div></div></div>
<p>Despite equal opportunity legislation, nursing has continued to be a female-dominated profession in many countries; according to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WHO" title="WHO">WHO</a>'s 2020 <i>State of the World's Nursing,</i> approximately 90% of the nursing workforce is female.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> For instance, the male-to-female ratio of nurses is approximately 1:19 in Canada and the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> This ratio is represented around the world. Notable exceptions include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francophone_Africa" title="Francophone Africa">Francophone Africa</a>, which includes the countries of Benin, Burkina Faso, Cameroon, Chad, Congo, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te_d%27Ivoire" title="Côte d'Ivoire">Côte d'Ivoire</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of Congo">Democratic Republic of Congo</a>, Djibouti, Guinea, Gabon, Mali, Mauritania, Niger, Rwanda, Senegal, and Togo, which all have more male than female nurses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MIN_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-MIN-59">[59]</a></sup> In Europe, in countries such as <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, over 20% of nurses are male.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MIN_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-MIN-59">[59]</a></sup> In the United Kingdom, 11% of nurses and midwives registered with the Nursing and Midwifery Council (NMC) are male.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> The number of male nurses in the United States doubled between 1980 and 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> However female nurses are still more common, but male nurses receive more pay on average.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup>
</p><p>Research has indicated that there can be negative effects of diversity within nursing. When there is a heavier focus on diversity in nursing, the quality of care or performance of the nurses can be hindered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Research demonstrates that as people begin to be different in a work setting, this can create issues if not addressed correctly. When hospitals begin to focus on diversity over their patients, the quality of care can be negatively affected if diversity becomes the main goal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Minorities_in_U.S._nursing">Minorities in U.S. nursing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Minorities in U.S. nursing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Statistically speaking, in the United States 19.2% of nursing positions are held by people of minority backgrounds. The remaining 80.8% of positions are held by Caucasian individuals, particularly women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Diversity in nursing is lacking.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Theory_and_process">Theory and process</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Theory and process">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Nursing_theory" title="Nursing theory">Nursing theory</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nursing_process" title="Nursing process">Nursing process</a></div>
<p>Nursing practice is the actual provision of nursing care. In providing care, nurses implement the <a href="/wiki/Nursing_care_plan" title="Nursing care plan">nursing care plan</a> using the <a href="/wiki/Nursing_process" title="Nursing process">nursing process</a>. This is based around a specific <a href="/wiki/Nursing_theory" title="Nursing theory">nursing theory</a> which is selected in consideration with the care setting and the population served. In providing nursing care, the nurse uses both nursing theory and best practice derived from <a href="/wiki/Nursing_research" title="Nursing research">nursing research</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weber2014_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-Weber2014-67">[67]</a></sup> The nursing process is made up of five steps: 1.evaluate, 2. implement, 3. plan, 4. diagnose, and 5. assess. Nurses are able to use this process from the American Nurses Association to determine the best care they can provide for the patient. There are many other diverse nursing theories as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-:3-68">[68]</a></sup>
</p><p>In general terms, the nursing process is the method used to <a href="/wiki/Nursing_assessment" title="Nursing assessment">assess</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nursing_diagnosis" title="Nursing diagnosis">diagnose</a> needs, plan outcomes and interventions, implement interventions, and evaluate the outcomes of the care provided. Like other disciplines, the profession has developed different theories derived from sometimes diverse philosophical beliefs and <a href="/wiki/Paradigm" title="Paradigm">paradigms</a> or <a href="/wiki/Worldview" title="Worldview">worldviews</a> to help nurses direct their activities to accomplish specific goals.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Scope_of_activities">Scope of activities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Scope of activities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Activities_of_daily_living_assistance">Activities of daily living assistance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Activities of daily living assistance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Activities_of_daily_living" title="Activities of daily living">Activities of daily living</a></div><p> Nurses manage and coordinate care to support activities of daily living (ADL). Often the provision of such care is delegated to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nursing_assistant" title="Nursing assistant">nursing assistants</a>. This includes assisting in patient mobility, such as moving an activity intolerant patient within bed.
</p><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medication">Medication</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Medication">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Medication management and administration are a part of most hospital nursing roles, however, prescribing authority varies between jurisdictions. In many areas, registered nurses administer and manage medications prescribed by a professional with full prescribing authority such as a <a href="/wiki/Nurse_practitioner" title="Nurse practitioner">nurse practitioner</a> or a <a href="/wiki/Physician" title="Physician">physician</a>. As nurses are responsible for evaluating patients throughout their care - including before and after medication administration - adjustments to medications are often made through a collaborative effort between the prescriber and the nurse. Regardless of the prescriber, nurses are legally responsible for the drugs they administer. There may be legal implications when there is an error in a prescription, and the nurse could be expected to have noted and reported the error. In the United States, nurses have the right to refuse any medication administration that they deem to be potentially harmful to the patient.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup>
In the United Kingdom there are some nurses who have taken additional specialist training that allows them to prescribe any medications from their scope of practice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rcn_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-rcn-70">[70]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Patient_education">Patient education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Patient education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Patient_education" title="Patient education">Patient education</a></div>
<p>The patient's family is often involved in the education. Effective patient education leads to fewer complications and hospital visits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> Many times, nurses are very busy and have a hard time giving information to the patient because they have so many other things going on. Educating the patient and their family increases the chance for a better patient experience.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Giving the best care requires informing the patient of what is going on and support. While explaining procedure, recovery, and taking care of the patient, nurses also have to help patients and their families cope with different medical situations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-:4-73">[73]</a></sup>
</p><p>When speaking with the patient, nurses have to be able to communicate in a way that can be understood by the patient. Informing the patient may involve speaking in broad, general terms, using visuals or different reading materials, and even including demonstrations if necessary. The more the patient and their family understand what the nurse is saying, the better healthcare the patient can receive without the assistance of a nurse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-:4-73">[73]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Specialties_and_practice_settings">Specialties and practice settings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Specialties and practice settings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_nursing_specialties" title="List of nursing specialties">List of nursing specialties</a></div>
<p>Nursing is the most diverse of all <a href="/wiki/Category:Health_care_occupations" title="Category:Health care occupations">health care professions</a>. Nurses practice in a wide range of settings but generally nursing is divided depending on the needs of the person being nursed.
</p><p>The major populations are:
</p>
<ul><li>communities/public</li>
<li>family/individual across the lifespan</li>
<li>adult-gerontology</li>
<li>pediatrics</li>
<li>neonatal</li>
<li>women's health/gender-related</li>
<li>mental health</li>
<li>informatics (<a href="/wiki/EHealth" title="EHealth">eHealth</a>)</li>
<li>acute care hospitals</li>
<li>ambulatory settings (physician offices, urgent care settings, camps, etc.)</li>
<li>school/college infirmaries</li></ul>
<p>Nurses with higher degrees allow for specialization within the medical field. There are many specific nursing professions that can be separated into categories of care type, age, gender, certain age group, practice setting, etc. Nurses are able to specialize with a combination of these categories as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-:5-1">[1]</a></sup> There are also specialist areas such as <a href="/wiki/Cardiac_nursing" title="Cardiac nursing">cardiac nursing</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orthopedic_nursing" title="Orthopedic nursing">orthopedic nursing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palliative_care" title="Palliative care">palliative care</a>, <a href="/wiki/Perioperative_nursing" title="Perioperative nursing">perioperative nursing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Obstetrical_nursing" title="Obstetrical nursing">obstetrical nursing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oncology_nursing" title="Oncology nursing">oncology nursing</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nursing_informatics" title="Nursing informatics">nursing informatics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Telenursing" title="Telenursing">telenursing</a>, radiology, and <a href="/wiki/Emergency_nursing" title="Emergency nursing">emergency nursing</a>.
</p><p>Nurses practice in a wide range of settings, including hospitals, private <a href="/wiki/Home_care" title="Home care">homes</a>, <a href="/wiki/School_nursing" title="School nursing">schools</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pharmaceutical_companies" title="Pharmaceutical companies">pharmaceutical companies</a>. Nurses work in <a href="/wiki/Occupational_health_nursing" title="Occupational health nursing">occupational health</a> settings<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> (also called industrial health settings), free-standing clinics and physician offices, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nurse-led_clinics" title="Nurse-led clinics">nurse-led clinics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Long-term_care" title="Long-term care">long-term care</a> facilities and camps. They also work on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cruise_ships" title="Cruise ships">cruise ships</a> and in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armed_Forces" title="Armed Forces">military service</a>. Nurses act as advisers and consultants to the health care and insurance industries. Many nurses also work in the <a href="/wiki/Health_advocacy" title="Health advocacy">health advocacy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Patient_advocacy" title="Patient advocacy">patient advocacy</a> fields at companies such as <a href="/wiki/Health_Advocate" title="Health Advocate">Health Advocate</a>, Inc. helping in a variety of clinical and administrative issues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Some are <a href="/wiki/Lawyer" title="Lawyer">attorneys</a> and others work with attorneys as <a href="/wiki/Legal_nurse_consultant" title="Legal nurse consultant">legal nurse consultants</a>, reviewing patient records to assure that adequate care was provided and testifying in court. Nurses can work on a temporary basis, which involves doing shifts without a contract in a variety of settings, sometimes known as <i>per diem nursing</i>, <i>agency nursing</i> or <i>travel nursing</i>. Nurses work as researchers in laboratories, universities, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Research_institutions" title="Research institutions">research institutions</a>. Nurses have also been delving into the world of informatics, acting as consultants to the creation of computerized charting programs and other software.  Nurse authors publish articles and books to provide essential reference materials.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Occupational_hazards">Occupational hazards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Occupational hazards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
