.mbox-text-span{margin-left:23px!important}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .ambox{margin:0 10%}}</style><table class="box-Speculation plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><img alt="" data-file-height="128" data-file-width="128" decoding="async" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Emoji_u1f52e.svg/40px-Emoji_u1f52e.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Emoji_u1f52e.svg/60px-Emoji_u1f52e.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Emoji_u1f52e.svg/80px-Emoji_u1f52e.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>possibly contains unsourced <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:CRYSTAL" title="Wikipedia:CRYSTAL">predictions</a>, speculative material, or accounts of events that might not occur</b>. Information must be <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:V" title="Wikipedia:V">verifiable</a> and based on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:RS" title="Wikipedia:RS">reliable published sources</a>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit">improve it</a> by removing unsourced speculative content.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">July 2012</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The International Council of Nursing (ICN), the largest international health professional organization in the world, recognizes the shortage of nurses as a growing crisis in the world. This shortage impacts the healthcare of everyone worldwide. One of the many reasons is that nurses who pursue to become nurses do so very late in their lives. This leads to a non-lengthy employment time. A national survey prepared by the Federation of Nurses and Health Professionals in 2001 found that one in five nurses plans to leave the profession within five years because of unsatisfactory working conditions, including low pay, severe under staffing, high stress, physical demands, mandatory overtime, and irregular hours. Approximately 29.8 percent of all nursing jobs are found in hospitals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bls.gov_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-bls.gov-91">[91]</a></sup> However, due to administrative cost cutting, increased nurse's workload, and rapid growth of outpatient services, hospital nursing jobs will experience slower than average growth. Employment in home care and nursing homes is expected<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (July 2012)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> to grow rapidly. Though more people are living well into their 80s and 90s, many need the kind of long-term care available at a nursing home. Many nurses will also be needed to help staff the growing number of out-patient facilities, such as HMOs (Health Maintenance Organizations), group medical practices, and ambulatory surgery centers. Nursing specialties will be in great demand. There are, in addition, many part-time employment possibilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-isbn0-8160-6587-X_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-isbn0-8160-6587-X-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nardi,_Deena_A._2013_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nardi,_Deena_A._2013-95">[95]</a></sup>
</p><p>Levsey, Campbell, and Green voiced their concern about the shortage of nurses, citing Fang, Wilsey-Wisniewski, &amp; Bednash, 2006, who state that over 40,000 qualified nursing applicants were turned away in the 2005–2006 academic year from baccalaureate nursing programs due to a lack of masters and doctoral qualified faculty, and that this number was increased over 9,000 from 32,000 qualified but rejected students from just two years earlier. Several strategies have been offered to mitigate this shortage including; Federal and private support for experienced nurses to enhance their education, incorporating more hybrid/blended nursing courses, and using simulation in lieu of clinical (hospital) training experiences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nardi,_Deena_A._2013_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-Nardi,_Deena_A._2013-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup>
</p><p>Furthermore, there is a shortage of academically qualified instructors to teach at schools of nursing worldwide. The serious need for educational capacity is not being met, which is the underlying most important preparation resource for the nurses of tomorrow. The decrease in faculty everywhere is due to many factors including decrease in satisfaction with the workforce, poor salaries, and reduction in full-time equivalent. Throughout the span of 6 years the nursing faculty shortage has been written about an increasing amount. There is no clear consensus or an organized plan on how to fix the ongoing issue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Continuing_education">Continuing education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Continuing education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>With health care knowledge growing steadily, nurses can stay ahead of the curve through continuing education. Continuing education classes and programs enable nurses to provide the best possible care to patients, advance nursing careers, and keep up with Board of Nursing requirements. The American Nurses Association and the American Nursing Credentialing Center are devoted to ensuring nurses have access to quality continuing education offerings. Continuing education classes are calibrated to provide enhanced learning for all levels of nurses. Many States also regulate Continuing Nursing Education. Nursing licensing boards requiring Continuing Nursing Education (CNE) as a condition for licensure, either initial or renewal, accept courses provided by organizations that are accredited by other state licensing boards, by the American Nursing Credentialing Center (ANCC), or by organizations that have been designated as an approver of continuing nursing education by ANCC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> There are some exceptions to this rule including the state of California, Florida and Kentucky. National Healthcare Institute<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nhinstitute_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-nhinstitute-99">[99]</a></sup> has created a list to assist nurses in determining their CNE credit hours requirements. While this list is not all inclusive, it offers details on how to contact nursing licensing boards directly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-http://www.nursingworld.org/_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-http://www.nursingworld.org/-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-http://www.NHInstitute.org/_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-http://www.NHInstitute.org/-101">[101]</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Board_certification">Board certification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Board certification">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Nursing_credentials_and_certifications" title="Nursing credentials and certifications">Nursing credentials and certifications</a></div>
<p>Professional nursing organizations, through their certification boards, have voluntary certification exams to demonstrate clinical competency in their particular specialty. Completion of the prerequisite work experience allows an RN to register for an examination, and passage gives an RN permission to use a professional designation after their name. For example, passage of the American Association of Critical-care Nurses specialty exam allows a nurse to use the initials 'CCRN' after his or her name. Other organizations and societies have similar procedures.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/American_Nurses_Credentialing_Center" title="American Nurses Credentialing Center">American Nurses Credentialing Center</a>, the credentialing arm of the <a href="/wiki/American_Nurses_Association" title="American Nurses Association">American Nurses Association</a>, is the largest nursing credentialing organization and administers more than 30 specialty examinations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ANCC_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-ANCC-102">[102]</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Correctional_nursing">Correctional nursing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Correctional nursing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Correctional_nursing" title="Correctional nursing">Correctional nursing</a></div>
<p>Due to its large <a href="/wiki/Incarceration_in_the_United_States" title="Incarceration in the United States">prison population</a>, the United States needs many <a href="/wiki/Correctional_nursing" title="Correctional nursing">correctional nurses</a> to help inmates receive proper health-care, including <a href="/wiki/Mentally_ill_people_in_United_States_jails_and_prisons" title="Mentally ill people in United States jails and prisons">mental health treatments for prisoners with psychological issues.</a> The demand for nurse is high everywhere. Nurses working in correctional care have to focus on the care of the patient, not what they did. They are to provide the best possible care because is a compassionate field and all nurses want is to better the patient.
</p><p>Nurses are not the only health care workers in correctional facilities. Some examples of people who work in correctional facilities are LPNS, RNs, nurse practitioners, doctors, pharmacists, therapists, and specialists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:52_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-:52-103">[103]</a></sup>
</p>
<h6><span class="mw-headline" id="Role_of_correctional_nurse">Role of correctional nurse</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Role of correctional nurse">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h6>
<p>When the individual arrives, nurses perform an initial exam that is just a basic checkup to determine what needs the patient may have while in prison. Here they can discover existing conditions or even signs of substance abuse. A correctional nurse can face a wide variety of healthcare issues including chronic medical conditions, mental health, infectious disease, and much more. Correctional nurses must follow stricter protocols then say in a hospital due to confidentiality. Assessing a patient can be difficult. A deputy or officer may have to be present during exams, which can make the patient feel restricted, and be less open with their medical information. Without the nurse knowing some information from the patient, prevent them from receiving the best care possible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:52_103-1"><a href="#cite_note-:52-103">[103]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Nursing_in_Canada" title="Nursing in Canada">Nursing in Canada</a></div>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="History_2">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Canadian nursing dates back to 1639 in <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a> with the Augustine nuns.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-test2_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-test2-104">[104]</a></sup> These nuns were trying to open a mission that cared for the spiritual and physical needs of patients. The establishment of this mission created the first nursing apprenticeship training in North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-test2_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-test2-104">[104]</a></sup> In the nineteenth century, some Catholic orders of nursing were trying to spread their message across Canada. Most nurses were female and only had an occasional consultation with a physician. Towards the end of the nineteenth century, hospital care and medical services had been improved and expanded. Much of this was due to Nightingale's influence. In 1874 the first formal nursing training program was started at the General and Marine Hospital in St. Catharines in Ontario.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-test2_104-2"><a href="#cite_note-test2-104">[104]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>All Canadian nurses and prospective nurses are heavily encouraged by the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Nurses_Association" title="Canadian Nurses Association">Canadian Nurses Association</a> to continue their education to receive a <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor's degree">bachelor's degree</a>. This degree may result in better patient outcomes.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> All Canadian provinces and territories, with the exception of the <a href="/wiki/Yukon" title="Yukon">Yukon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>, require that all nurses have a bachelor's degree.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-test2_104-3"><a href="#cite_note-test2-104">[104]</a></sup> The length of time generally required to obtain this degree is four years. However, some Canadian universities offer a condensed program that is two years in length.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-test2_104-4"><a href="#cite_note-test2-104">[104]</a></sup>
</p><p>Nursing specialty certification is available through the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Nurses_Association" title="Canadian Nurses Association">Canadian Nurses Association</a> in 22 practice areas,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-test2_104-5"><a href="#cite_note-test2-104">[104]</a></sup> including:
</p>
<ul><li>cardiovascular nursing</li>
<li>community health nursing</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Critical_care_nursing" title="Critical care nursing">critical care nursing</a></li>
<li>pediatric critical care nursing</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Emergency_nursing" title="Emergency nursing">emergency nursing</a></li>
<li>gastroenterology nursing</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gerontological_nursing" title="Gerontological nursing">gerontological nursing</a></li>
<li>hospice palliative care nursing</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Medical-surgical_nursing" title="Medical-surgical nursing">medical-surgical nursing</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Neonatal_nursing" title="Neonatal nursing">neonatal nursing</a></li>
<li>nephrology nursing</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Neuroscience_nursing" title="Neuroscience nursing">neuroscience nursing</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Occupational_health_nursing" title="Occupational health nursing">occupational health nursing</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Oncology_nursing" title="Oncology nursing">oncology nursing</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orthopedic_nursing" title="Orthopedic nursing">orthopedic nursing</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pediatric_nursing" title="Pediatric nursing">pediatric nursing</a></li>
<li>peri-anesthesia nursing</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Obstetrical_nursing" title="Obstetrical nursing">obstetrical nursing</a></li>
<li>peri-operative nursing</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Psychiatric_and_mental_health_nursing" title="Psychiatric and mental health nursing">psychiatric and mental health nursing</a></li>
<li>rehabilitation nursing</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wound,_ostomy,_and_continence_nursing" title="Wound, ostomy, and continence nursing">Wound, ostomy, and continence nursing</a></li></ul>
<p>Nursing specialty certification generally requires practice, experience, and passing a test that is based on competencies for that specific medical or surgical domain in which nursing care is provided. The certification in gerontological nursing, which involves providing care to the elderly, is offered to not only RNs and NPs but also LPNs.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Latin_America">Latin America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Latin America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Latin American nursing is based on three levels of training: (a) professional/registered, (b) technical, and (c) auxiliary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> The nursing education in Latin America and the Caribbean includes the principles and values of the Universal Health and primary health care. These principles underpin transformative education modalities such as critical and complex thinking development, problem-solving, evidence-based clinical decision-making, and lifelong learning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> The Pan American Health Organization/World Health Organization (PAHO/WHO) proposes the Strategy for Universal Access to Health and Universal Health Coverage to improve health outcomes and other basic objectives of health systems based on the right of each person to receive the best standard of health, without exposing people to financial difficulties through nursing intervention.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Spain">Spain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Spain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>See <a href="/wiki/Nursing_in_Spain" title="Nursing in Spain">Nursing in Spain</a>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Nursing_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Nursing in the United Kingdom">Nursing in the United Kingdom</a></div>
<p>To practice lawfully as a registered nurse in the United Kingdom, the practitioner must hold a current and valid registration with the <a href="/wiki/Nursing_and_Midwifery_Council" title="Nursing and Midwifery Council">Nursing and Midwifery Council</a>. The title "Registered Nurse" can only be granted to those holding such registration. This protected title is laid down in the Nurses, Midwives and Health Visitors Act, 1997.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ACT2_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-ACT2-108">[108]</a></sup> From April 2016, nurses in the United Kingdom are expected to revalidate every three years which involves providing evidence of further development and active practice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="First_and_second_level">First and second level</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: First and second level">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>First-level nurses make up the bulk of the registered nurses in the UK. They were previously known by titles such as Registered General Nurse (RGN), Registered Sick Children's Nurse (RSCN), Registered Mental Nurse (RMN), and Registered Nurse (for the) Mentally Handicapped (RNMH). The titles used now are similar, including Registered Nurse Adult (RNA), Registered Nurse Child (RNC), Registered Nurse Mental Health (RNMH), and Registered Nurse (of) Learning Disabilities (RNLD). Second-level nurse training is no longer provided; however, they are still legally able to practice in the United Kingdom as a registered nurse. Many have now either retired or undertaken conversion courses to become first-level nurses. They are entitled to refer to themselves as registered nurses as their registration is on the Nursing &amp; Midwifery Council register of nurses, although most refer to themselves as Enrolled Nurses (ENs) or State Enrolled Nurses (SENs).
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Advanced_practice">Advanced practice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Advanced practice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<ul><li><i>Nurse practitioners</i> – Most of these nurses obtain a minimum of a master's degree and a desired post grad certificate. They often perform roles similar to those of physicians and physician assistants. They can prescribe medications as independent or supplementary prescribers, although they are still legally regulated, unlike physician's assistants. Most Nurse Practitioners (NPs) have referral and admission rights to hospital specialties. They commonly work in <a href="/wiki/Primary_care" title="Primary care">primary care</a> (e.g. General Practitioner (GP) surgeries), <a href="/wiki/Emergency_department" title="Emergency department">Accident and Emergency (A&amp;E) departments</a>, or pediatrics although they are increasingly being seen in other areas of practice. In the UK, the title "nurse practitioner" is legally protected.</li>
<li><i>Specialist community public health nurses</i> – traditionally <a href="/wiki/District_nurse" title="District nurse">district nurses</a> and <a href="/wiki/Health_visitor" title="Health visitor">health visitors</a>, this group oversees research and publication activities.</li>
<li><i>Lecturer-practitioners (also called practice education facilitators)</i> – these nurses work both in the National Health Service (NHS), and in universities. They typically work 2–3 days per week in each setting. In university, they train pre-registration student nurses (see below), and often teach on specialist courses post-registration nurses.</li>
<li><i>Lecturers</i> – these nurses are not employed by the NHS. Instead they work full-time in universities, both teaching and performing research.</li></ul>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Managers">Managers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Managers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Many nurses who have worked in clinical settings for a long time choose to leave clinical nursing and join the ranks of the NHS management. This used to be seen as a natural career progression for those who had reached ward management positions, however with the advent of specialist nursing roles (see above), this has become a less attractive option.
</p><p>Nonetheless, many nurses fill positions in the senior management structure of NHS organizations, some even as board members. Others choose to stay a little closer to their clinical roots by becoming clinical nurse managers or <i><a href="/wiki/Matron" title="Matron">modern matrons</a></i>.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Nurse_education">Nurse education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Nurse education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<h6><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-registration">Pre-registration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Pre-registration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h6>
<p>To become a registered nurse, one must complete a program recognised by the <a href="/wiki/Nursing_and_Midwifery_Council" title="Nursing and Midwifery Council">Nursing and Midwifery Council</a> (NMC). Currently, this involves completing a <a href="/wiki/Academic_degree" title="Academic degree">degree</a>, available from a range of <a href="/wiki/Category:Nursing_schools_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Category:Nursing schools in the United Kingdom">universities offering these courses</a>, in the chosen branch specialty (see below), leading to both an academic award and professional registration as a 1st level registered nurse. Such a course is a 50/50 split of learning in university (i.e. through lectures, assignments and examinations) and in practice (i.e. supervised patient care within a hospital or community setting).
</p><p>These courses are three (occasionally four) years' long. The first year is known as the common foundation program (CFP), and teaches the basic knowledge and skills required of all nurses. Skills included in the CFP may include communication, taking observations, administering medication and providing personal care to patients. The remainder of the program consists of training specific to the student's chosen branch of nursing. These are:
</p>
<ul><li>Child nursing</li>
<li>Mental health nursing</li>
<li>Learning disabilities nursing</li></ul>
<p>As of 2013, the Nursing and Midwifery Council will require all new nurses qualifying in the UK to hold a degree qualification.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-http://www.nmc-uk.org/Get-involved/Consultations/Past-consultations/By-year/Pre-registration-nursing-education-Phase-2/Changes-to-pre-registration-nursing-programmes-FAQs-/2_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-http://www.nmc-uk.org/Get-involved/Consultations/Past-consultations/By-year/Pre-registration-nursing-education-Phase-2/Changes-to-pre-registration-nursing-programmes-FAQs-/2-111">[111]</a></sup> However, those nurses who hold a diploma, or even a certificate in nursing are still able to legally practice in the UK, although they are able to undertake university modules to obtain enough credits to top up to a degree.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Midwifery" title="Midwifery">Midwifery</a> training is similar in length and structure, but is sufficiently different that it is not considered a branch of nursing. There are shortened (18-month) programs to allow nurses already qualified in the adult branch to hold dual registration as a nurse and a midwife. Shortened courses lasting 2 years also exist for graduates of other disciplines to train as nurses. This is achieved by more intense study and a shortening of the common foundation program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NMC2_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-NMC2-112">[112]</a></sup>
</p><p>As of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> student nurses in England and Wales can apply for a <a href="/wiki/Bursary" title="Bursary">bursary</a> from the government to support them during their nurse training, and may also be eligible for a student loan, although there has been speculation that this will not be available in the future.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nursingtimes2_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-nursingtimes2-113">[113]</a></sup> Student nurses in Scotland still receive a standard bursary which is not means tested, and their tuition fees continue to be paid – however, they are not eligible for student loans.
</p><p>Before Project 2000, nurse education was the responsibility of hospitals and was not based in universities; hence many nurses who qualified prior to these reforms do not hold an academic award.
</p>
<h6><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-registration">Post-registration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Post-registration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h6>
<p>After the point of initial registration, there is an expectation that all qualified nurses will continue to update their skills and knowledge. The Nursing and Midwifery Council insists on a minimum of 35 hours of education every three years, as part of its post registration education and practice (PREP) requirements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-http://www.nmc-uk.org/Nurses-and-midwives/Advice-by-topic/A/Advice/Post-Registration-Education-and-Practice-Prep-requirements-for-midwives/2_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-http://www.nmc-uk.org/Nurses-and-midwives/Advice-by-topic/A/Advice/Post-Registration-Education-and-Practice-Prep-requirements-for-midwives/2-114">[114]</a></sup>
</p><p>There are also opportunities for many nurses to gain additional clinical skills after qualification. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cannulation" title="Cannulation">Cannulation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venipuncture" title="Venipuncture">venipuncture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Intravenous_therapy" title="Intravenous therapy">intravenous drug therapy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Urinary_catheterization" title="Urinary catheterization">male catheterization</a> are the most common, although there are many others (such as <a href="/wiki/Advanced_life_support" title="Advanced life support">advanced life support</a>), which some nurses undertake.
</p><p>Many nurses who qualified with a diploma choose to upgrade their qualification to a degree by studying part-time. Many nurses prefer this option to gaining a degree initially, as there is often an opportunity to study in a specialist field as a part of this upgrading. Financially, in England, it was also much more lucrative, as diploma students get the full bursary during their initial training, and employers often pay for the degree course as well as the nurse's salary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nursing_and_Midwifery_Education,_20072_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nursing_and_Midwifery_Education,_20072-115">[115]</a></sup>
</p><p>To become specialist nurses (such as nurse consultants, nurse practitioners etc.) or nurse educators, some nurses undertake further training above bachelor's degree level. Master's degrees exist in various healthcare related topics, and some nurses choose to study for PhDs or other higher academic awards. <a href="/wiki/District_nurse" title="District nurse">District nurses</a> and <a href="/wiki/Health_visitor" title="Health visitor">health visitors</a> are also considered specialist nurses, and to become such they must undertake specialist training. This is a one-year full-time degree.
</p><p>All newly qualifying <a href="/wiki/District_nurse" title="District nurse">district nurses</a> and <a href="/wiki/Health_visitor" title="Health visitor">health visitors</a> are trained to prescribe from the Nurse Prescribers' Formulary, a list of medications and dressings typically useful to those carrying out these roles. Many of these (and other) nurses will also undertake training in independent and supplementary prescribing, which allows them (as of 1 May 2006) to prescribe almost any drug in the <a href="/wiki/British_National_Formulary" title="British National Formulary">British National Formulary</a>. This has been the cause of a great deal of debate in both medical and nursing circles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BFN2_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-BFN2-116">[116]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Union">European Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: European Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the European Union, the profession of nurse is regulated. A profession is said to be regulated when access and exercise is subject to the possession of a specific professional qualification. The regulated professions database contains a list of regulated professions for nurse<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-europa2_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-europa2-117">[117]</a></sup> in the European Union (EU) member states, European Economic Area (EEA) countries, and Switzerland. This list is covered by the Directive 2005/36/EC.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia">Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Nursing education is governed in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> by the central body <a href="/wiki/Indian_Nursing_Council" title="Indian Nursing Council">Indian Nursing Council</a> and its norms are implemented through respective State Nursing councils. The list of state nursing councils are available in the official web page of Indian Nursing Council. First formal education in nursing was offered in Madras Medical college, in Madras presidency. 
Indian Nursing Council Act, 1947. Act Year Number: Act No. 19 of December enactment Date of enactment: [31 December 19act] Act Objective: An Act to constitute the Nursing Council of India. To establish uniform standards of training for nurses, midwives, and health visitors. It is implemented with 17 sections and each section indicates the specific legislative role of the council.
</p><p>The nursing profession was dominated by females in the British colonial period, but in Madras Presidency, men were actively engaged in the profession.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Iran">Iran</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Iran">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Nursing_in_Iran" title="Nursing in Iran">Nursing in Iran</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Israel">Israel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Israel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Nurses in <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> have a wide variety of responsibilities, including hospital care, patient education, wound care, prenatal and other monitoring, midwifery, and well-baby clinics.
</p><p>Nursing in Israeli Jewish culture traces its origins to <a href="/wiki/Shiphrah_and_Puah" title="Shiphrah and Puah">Shifra and Puah</a>, two <a href="/wiki/Hebrews" title="Hebrews">Hebrew</a> midwives depicted in the <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Exodus" title="Book of Exodus">Book of Exodus</a> helping women in ancient Egypt give birth and keep their infants safe.
</p><p>Modern-day nursing was established by nurses sent to <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine" title="Mandatory Palestine">Mandatory Palestine</a> and later Israel by the <a href="/wiki/Hadassah_Women%27s_Zionist_Organization_of_America" title="Hadassah Women's Zionist Organization of America">Hadassah</a> organization, as well as a nursing school founded by <a href="/wiki/Henrietta_Szold" title="Henrietta Szold">Henrietta Szold</a> in 1918.  During those times, the United Kingdom regulated midwifery in Mandatory Palestine, but the nurses were not mentioned in the regulation decree.
</p><p>Today, nurses and midwives are regulated by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli_Ministry_of_Health" title="Israeli Ministry of Health">Israeli Ministry of Health</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Japan">Japan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Japan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Nursing_in_Japan" title="Nursing in Japan">Nursing in Japan</a></div>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="History_3">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Nursing was not an established part of Japan's healthcare system until 1899 with the Midwives Ordinance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nurse3_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-nurse3-119">[119]</a></sup> From there the Registered Nurse Ordinance came into play in 1915. This established a legal substantiation to registered nurses all over Japan. A new law geared towards nurses was created during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>: the <i>Public Health Nurse, Midwife and Nurse Law</i>, established in 1948.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-test2_104-6"><a href="#cite_note-test2-104">[104]</a></sup> It established educational requirements, standards and licensure. There has been a continued effort to improve nursing in Japan. In 1992 the Nursing Human Resource Law was passed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-test2_104-7"><a href="#cite_note-test2-104">[104]</a></sup> This law created the development of new university programs for nurses. Those programs were designed to raise the education level of the nurses so that they could be better suited for taking care of the public.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Types_of_nurses">Types of nurses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Types of nurses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Japan only recognizes four types of nursing and they are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_Health_Nursing" title="Public Health Nursing">Public Health Nursing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Midwifery" title="Midwifery">Midwifery</a>, Registered Nursing and Assistant Nursing.
</p>
<h6><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_health">Public health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Public health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h6>
<p>This type of nursing is designed to help the public and is also driven by the public's needs. The goals of public health nurses are to monitor the spread of disease, keep vigilant watch for environmental hazards, educate the community on how to care for and treat themselves, and train for community disasters.
</p>
<h6><span class="mw-headline" id="Midwifery">Midwifery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Midwifery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h6>
<p>Nurses that are involved with midwifery are independent of any organization. A <a href="/wiki/Midwife" title="Midwife">midwife</a> takes care of a pregnant woman during labour and postpartum. They assist with things like breastfeeding and caring for the child.
</p>
<h6><span class="mw-headline" id="Nursing_assistant">Nursing assistant</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Nursing assistant">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h6>
<p>Nursing assistants, also known as nurse assistants or CNAs (Certified Nursing Assistants), assist patients with basic daily tasks. Individuals who are assistant nurses follow orders from a registered nurse. They report back to the licensed nurse about a patient's condition. Assistant nurses are always supervised by a licensed registered nurse.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_2">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>In 1952 Japan established the first nursing university in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-test2_104-8"><a href="#cite_note-test2-104">[104]</a></sup> An <a href="/wiki/Associate_of_Science_in_Nursing" title="Associate of Science in Nursing">associate degree</a> was the only level of certification for years. Soon people began to want nursing degrees at a higher level of education. Soon the <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Science_in_Nursing" title="Bachelor of Science in Nursing">Bachelor's Degree in Nursing</a> (BSN) was established. Currently, Japan offers <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doctorate_in_Nursing" title="Doctorate in Nursing">doctorate</a>-level degrees of nursing in a good number of its universities.
</p><p>There are three ways that an individual could become a registered nurse in Japan. After obtaining a high school degree the person could go to a nursing university for four years and earn a bachelor's degree, go to a junior nursing college for three years or go to a nursing school for three years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-test2_104-9"><a href="#cite_note-test2-104">[104]</a></sup> Regardless of where the individual attends school they must take the national exam. Those who attended a nursing university have a bit of an advantage over those who went to a nursing school. They can take the national exam to be a registered nurse, public health nurse or midwife. In the cases of becoming a midwife or a public health nurse, the student must take a one-year course in their desired field after attending a nursing university and passing the national exam to become a registered nurse. The nursing universities are the best route for someone who wants to become a nurse in Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-test2_104-10"><a href="#cite_note-test2-104">[104]</a></sup> They offer a wider range of general education classes and they also allow for a more rigid teaching style of nursing. These nursing universities train their students to be able to make critical and educated decisions when they are out in the field. Physicians are the ones who are teaching the potential nurses because there are not enough available nurses to teach students. This increases the dominance that physicians have over nurses.
</p><p>Students that attend a nursing college or just a nursing school receive the same degree as one who graduated from a nursing university would, but they do not have the same educational background. The classes offered at nursing colleges and nursing schools are focused on more practical aspects of nursing. These institutions do not offer many general education classes, so students who attend these schools will solely be focusing on their nursing educations while they are in school. Students who attend a nursing college or school do have the opportunity to become a <a href="/wiki/Midwife" title="Midwife">midwife</a> or a public health nurse. They have to go through a training institute for their desired field after graduating from the nursing school or college.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-test2_104-11"><a href="#cite_note-test2-104">[104]</a></sup> Japanese nurses never have to renew their licenses. Once they have passed their exam, they have their license for life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-test2_104-12"><a href="#cite_note-test2-104">[104]</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Today">Today</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Today">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Like the United States, Japan is in need of more nurses. The driving force behind this need is the fact that country is aging and needs more medical care for its people. However, the number of available nurses does not seem to be increasing. Nurses face poor working conditions and low social status, and there is a cultural idea that married women quit their jobs for family responsibilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nurse22_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-nurse22-120">[120]</a></sup> On average, Japanese nurses make around 280,000 yen a month, and it is one of the higher paying jobs. However, physicians make twice as much as nurses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-worldsalaries2_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-worldsalaries2-121">[121]</a></sup> Similar to other cultures, the Japanese people view nurses as subservient to physicians. According to the <a href="/wiki/American_Nurses_Association" title="American Nurses Association">American Nurses Association</a> article on Japan, "nursing work has been described using negative terminology such as 'hard, dirty, dangerous, low salary, few holidays, minimal chance of marriage and family, and poor image.'"
</p><p>There are organizations that unite Japanese nurses like the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Nursing_Association" title="Japanese Nursing Association">Japanese Nursing Association</a> (JNA); the JNA is a professional organization and not a union. Members of the JNA lobby politicians and produces publications about nursing. According to the American Nurses Association's article on Japan, the JNA "works toward the improvement in nursing practice through many activities including the development of a policy research group to influence policy development, a code of ethics for nurses, and standards of nursing practice." The JNA also provides certification for specialists in mental health, oncology and community health.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-test2_104-13"><a href="#cite_note-test2-104">[104]</a></sup> There are other organizations, including some that categorize nurses by specialty, like emergency nursing or disaster nursing. One of the older unions that relates to nursing is the Japanese Federation of Medical Workers Union, which was created in 1957.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-test2_104-14"><a href="#cite_note-test2-104">[104]</a></sup> It is a union that includes physicians as well as nurses. This organization was involved with the <b>Nursing Human Resource Law</b>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-test2_104-15"><a href="#cite_note-test2-104">[104]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Taiwan">Taiwan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Taiwan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Nursing_in_Taiwan" title="Nursing in Taiwan">Nursing in Taiwan</a></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Health_and_Welfare_(Taiwan)" title="Ministry of Health and Welfare (Taiwan)">Ministry of Health and Welfare</a> is in charge of the regulation of nursing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> The Taiwan Union of Nurses Association (TUNA) is the union unit in Taiwan, fighting for nurses on payment and working time issues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">Australia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Australia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Nursing_in_Australia" title="Nursing in Australia">Nursing in Australia</a></div>
<p>Catholic religious institutes were influential in the development of Australian nursing, founding many of Australia's hospitals – the Irish <a href="/wiki/Sisters_of_Charity_of_Australia" title="Sisters of Charity of Australia">Sisters of Charity</a> were first to arrive in 1838 and established <a href="/wiki/St_Vincent%27s_Hospital,_Sydney" title="St Vincent's Hospital, Sydney">St Vincent's Hospital, Sydney</a> in 1857 as a free hospital for the poor. They and other orders like the <a href="/wiki/Sisters_of_Mercy" title="Sisters of Mercy">Sisters of Mercy</a>, and in aged care the Sisters of the Little Company of Mary and <a href="/wiki/Little_Sisters_of_the_Poor" title="Little Sisters of the Poor">Little Sisters of the Poor</a> founded hospitals, hospices, research institutes and aged care facilities around Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup>
</p><p>A census in the 1800s found several hundred nurses working in Western Australia during the colonial period of history, this included Aboriginal female servants who cared for the infirm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup>
</p><p>The state nursing licensing bodies amalgamated in Australia in 2011 under the federal body AHPRA (Australian Health Practitioner Registration Authority).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> Several divisions of nursing license is available and recognized around the country.
</p>
<ul><li>Enrolled nurses may initiate some oral medication orders with a specific competency now included in national curricula but variable in application by agency.</li>
<li>Registered nurses hold a university degree (enrolled nurses can progress to registered nurse status and do get credit for previous study).</li>
<li>Nurse practitioners have started emerging from postgraduate programs and work in both private practice and <a href="/wiki/Public_hospital" title="Public hospital">public hospitals and clinics</a>.</li>
<li>Mental health nurses must complete further training as advanced mental health practitioners in order to administer client referrals under the <i>Mental Health Act</i>.</li></ul>
<p>Australia enjoys the luxury of a national curriculum for vocational nurses, trained at Technical and Further Education (TAFE) colleges or private Registered Training Organization (RTO). Enrolled and registered nurses are identified by the department of immigration as an occupational area of need, although registered nurses are always in shorter supply, and this increases in proportion with specialization.
</p><p><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1986 there were a number of rolling industrial actions around the country, culminating when five thousand Victorian nurses went on strike for eighteen days. The hospitals were able to function by hiring casual staff from each other's striking members, but the increased cost forced a decision in the nurses' favor.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical">Historical</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=65" title="Edit section: Historical">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<li>Dock, Lavinia Lloyd. <i>A Short history of nursing from the earliest times to the present day</i> (1920) <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=IqC09J62exQC" rel="nofollow">full text online</a>; abbreviated version of her four volume <i>A History of Nursing</i> <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=uiJtAAAAMAAJ" rel="nofollow">vol 3 online</a></li>
<li>Donahue, M. Patricia. <i>Nursing, The Finest Art: An Illustrated History</i> (3rd ed. 2010), includes over 400 illustrations; 416pp; <a class="external text" href="https://www.amazon.com/dp/032305305X/" rel="nofollow">excerpt and text search</a></li>
